Keep the pancakes hot on steam, or covered in the oven. <NEXT_INSTR> Cold pancakes are awful! <NEXT_INSTR> The following recipe is a luxury one, for special occasions, as many eggs are used in preparing (instead of yeast). <INSTR_END> <TITLE_START> Colonial Cheese Biscuits <TITLE_END> <RECIPE_END>

<RECIPE_ START> <INPUT_START> baking potatoes <NEXT_INPUT> extra lean ground beef <NEXT_INPUT> butter <NEXT_INPUT> milk <NEXT_INPUT> salt <NEXT_INPUT> pepper <NEXT_INPUT> Cheddar cheese <NEXT_INPUT> bacon <NEXT_INPUT> green onion <NEXT_INPUT> sour cream <INPUT_END> <INGR_START> 6 baking potatoes <NEXT_INGR> 1 lb. of extra lean ground beef <NEXT_INGR> 2/3 c. butter or margarine <NEXT_INGR> 6 c. milk <NEXT_INGR> 3/4 tsp. salt <NEXT_INGR> 1/2 tsp. pepper <NEXT_INGR> 1 1/2 c (6 oz.) shredded Cheddar cheese, divided <NEXT_INGR> 12 sliced bacon, cooked, crumbled and divided <NEXT_INGR> 4 green onion, chopped and divided <NEXT_INGR> 1 (8 oz.) carton sour cream (optional) <INGR_END> <INSTR_START> Wash potatoes; prick several times with a fork. <NEXT_INSTR> Microwave them with a wet paper towel covering the potatoes on high for 6-8 minutes. <NEXT_INSTR> The potatoes should be soft, ready to eat. <NEXT_INSTR> Let them cool enough to handle. <NEXT_INSTR> Cut in half lengthwise; scoop out pulp and reserve. <NEXT_INSTR> Discard shells. <NEXT_INSTR> Brown ground beef until done. <NEXT_INSTR> Drain any grease from the meat. <NEXT_INSTR> Set aside when done. <NEXT_INSTR> Meat will be added later. <NEXT_INSTR> Melt butter in a large kettle over low heat; add flour, stirring until smooth. <NEXT_INSTR> Cook 1 minute, stirring constantly. Gradually add milk; cook over medium heat, stirring constantly, until thickened and bubbly. <NEXT_INSTR> Stir in potato, ground beef, salt, pepper, 1 cup of cheese, 2 tablespoons of green onion and 1/2 cup of bacon. <NEXT_INSTR> Cook until heated (do not boil). <NEXT_INSTR> Stir in sour cream if desired; cook until heated (do not boil). <NEXT_INSTR> Sprinkle with remaining cheese, bacon and green onions. <INSTR_END> <TITLE_START> Cheeseburger Potato Soup <TITLE_END> <RECIPE_END>

<RECIPE_ START> <INPUT_START> unsalted butter <NEXT_INPUT> sugar <NEXT_INPUT> vanilla <NEXT_INPUT> flour <NEXT_INPUT> walnuts <NEXT_INPUT> powdered sugar <INPUT_END> <INGR_START> 1 stick unsalted butter (room temperature) <NEXT_INGR> 2 Tbsp. granulated sugar <NEXT_INGR> 1 tsp. vanilla <NEXT_INGR> 1 c. all-purpose flour, sifted <NEXT_INGR> 1 c. finely chopped walnuts <NEXT_INGR> 1 c. powdered sugar, sifted <INGR_END> <INSTR_START> Preheat oven to 300°. Line 2 cookie sheets with parchment paper or leave them ungreased. Cream the butter, sugar and vanilla until light and fluffy. Add the flour and mix on low speed until very well blended. Add the nuts and mix well until well blended. Measure out generously rounded teaspoonfuls of dough and roll them into balls with your hands. Place about 2-inches apart on the prepared cookie sheets. Bake the cookies until they begin to turn golden, about 30 minutes. To test for doneness, remove 1 from sheet and cut in half. There should be no doughy strip in the center. <RECIPE_ START> <INPUT_START> flour <NEXT_INPUT> walnuts <NEXT_INPUT> toasted wheat germ <NEXT_INPUT> brown sugar <NEXT_INPUT> baking powder <NEXT_INPUT> cinnamon <NEXT_INPUT> salt <NEXT_INPUT> ground nutmeg <NEXT_INPUT> bananas <NEXT_INPUT> milk <NEXT_INPUT> butter <NEXT_INPUT> egg <NEXT_INPUT> cinnamon sugar <INPUT_END> <INGR_START> 1 1/2 c. whole-wheat flour <NEXT_INGR> 1 c. chopped walnuts <NEXT_INGR> 1/2 c. toasted wheat germ <NEXT_INGR> 1/2 c. brown sugar <NEXT_INGR> 1 Tbsp. baking powder <NEXT_INGR> 1 tsp. cinnamon <NEXT_INGR> 1/2 tsp. salt <NEXT_INGR> 1/4 tsp. ground nutmeg <NEXT_INGR> 2 ripe bananas, mashed <NEXT_INGR> 3/4 c. milk <NEXT_INGR> 5 Tbsp. melted butter <NEXT_INGR> 1 egg <NEXT_INGR> cinnamon sugar (optional) <INGR_END> <INSTR_START> Preheat oven to 400°. <NEXT_INSTR> Fit 12 muffin cups with paper liners. Coat each with cooking spray. <NEXT_INSTR> Mix flour, walnuts, wheat germ, brown sugar, baking powder, cinnamon, salt and nutmeg in large bowl. <NEXT_INSTR> Stir in bananas, milk, butter and egg. <NEXT_INSTR> Mix just until blended. <NEXT_INSTR> Using an ice cream scoop, fill muffin cups evenly with batter. <NEXT_INSTR> Sprinkle with cinnamon sugar, if desired. <NEXT_INSTR> Bake muffins until a skewer inserted into centers comes out clean, 20 to 22 minutes. <NEXT_INSTR> Cool 1 minute, then remove from the muffin pan and cool on a wire rack. Makes 1 dozen muffins. <INSTR_END> <TITLE_START> Banana Nut Muffins <TITLE_END> <RECIPE_END>
<RECIPE_ START> <INPUT_START> pear halves <NEXT_INPUT> lime gelatin <NEXT_INPUT> cream cheese <NEXT_INPUT> lemon yogurt <INPUT_END> <INGR_START> 1 (16 oz.) can pear halves, undrained <NEXT_INGR> 1 (3 oz.) pkg. lime gelatin <NEXT_INGR> 1 (8 oz.) pkg. cream cheese, softened <NEXT_INGR> 1 (8 oz.) carton lemon yogurt <INGR_END> <INSTR_START> Drain pears, reserving juice. <NEXT_INSTR> Bring juice to a boil, stirring constantly. <NEXT_INSTR> Remove from heat. <NEXT_INSTR> Add gelatin, stirring until dissolved. <NEXT_INSTR> Let cool slightly. <NEXT_INSTR> Coarsely chop pear halves. Combine cream cheese and yogurt; beat at medium speed of electric mixer until smooth. <NEXT_INSTR> Add gelatin and beat well. <NEXT_INSTR> Stir in pears. <NEXT_INSTR> Pour into an oiled 4-cup mold or Pyrex dish. <NEXT_INSTR> Chill. <INSTR_END> <TITLE_START> Pear-Lime Salad <TITLE_END> <RECIPE_END>
